    5861             : 
    5862             : /*
    5863             :  * When the PL/pgSQL parser expects to see a SQL statement, it is very
    5864             :  * liberal in what it accepts; for example, we often assume an
    5865             :  * unrecognized keyword is the beginning of a SQL statement. This
    5866             :  * avoids the need to duplicate parts of the SQL grammar in the
    5867             :  * PL/pgSQL grammar, but it means we can accept wildly malformed
    5868             :  * input. To try and catch some of the more obviously invalid input,
    5869             :  * we run the strings we expect to be SQL statements through the main
    5870             :  * SQL parser.
    5871             :  *
    5872             :  * We only invoke the raw parser (not the analyzer); this doesn't do
    5873             :  * any database access and does not check any semantic rules, it just
    5874             :  * checks for basic syntactic correctness. We do this here, rather
    5875             :  * than after parsing has finished, because a malformed SQL statement
    5876             :  * may cause the PL/pgSQL parser to become confused about statement
    5877             :  * borders. So it is best to bail out as early as we can.
    5878             :  *
    5879             :  * It is assumed that "stmt" represents a copy of the function source text
    5880             :  * beginning at offset "location".  We use this assumption to transpose
    5881             :  * any error cursor position back to the function source text.
    5882             :  * If no error cursor is provided, we'll just point at "location".
    5883             :  */
    5884             : static void
    5885             : check_sql_expr(const char *stmt, RawParseMode parseMode, int location)
    5886             : {
    5887             :     sql_error_callback_arg cbarg;
    5888             :     ErrorContextCallback  syntax_errcontext;
    5889             :     MemoryContext oldCxt;
    5890             : 
    5891             :     if (!plpgsql_check_syntax)
    5892             :         return;
    5893             : 
    5894             :     cbarg.location = location;
    5895             : 
    5896             :     syntax_errcontext.callback = plpgsql_sql_error_callback;
    5897             :     syntax_errcontext.arg = &cbarg;
    5898             :     syntax_errcontext.previous = error_context_stack;
    5899             :     error_context_stack = &syntax_errcontext;
    5900             : 
    5901             :     oldCxt = MemoryContextSwitchTo(plpgsql_compile_tmp_cxt);
    5902             :     (void) raw_parser(stmt, parseMode);
    5903             :     MemoryContextSwitchTo(oldCxt);
    5904             : 
    5905             :     /* Restore former ereport callback */
    5906             :     error_context_stack = syntax_errcontext.previous;
    5907             : }
    5908             : 
    5909             : static void
    5910             : plpgsql_sql_error_callback(void *arg)
    5911             : {
    5912             :     sql_error_callback_arg *cbarg = (sql_error_callback_arg *) arg;
    5913             :     int         errpos;
    5914             : 
    5915             :     /*
    5916             :      * First, set up internalerrposition to point to the start of the
    5917             :      * statement text within the function text.  Note this converts
    5918             :      * location (a byte offset) to a character number.
    5919             :      */
    5920             :     parser_errposition(cbarg->location);
    5921             : 
    5922             :     /*
    5923             :      * If the core parser provided an error position, transpose it.
    5924             :      * Note we are dealing with 1-based character numbers at this point.
    5925             :      */
    5926             :     errpos = geterrposition();
    5927             :     if (errpos > 0)
    5928             :     {
    5929             :         int         myerrpos = getinternalerrposition();
    5930             : 
    5931             :         if (myerrpos > 0)        /* safety check */
    5932             :             internalerrposition(myerrpos + errpos - 1);
    5933             :     }
    5934             : 
    5935             :     /* In any case, flush errposition --- we want internalerrposition only */
    5936             :     errposition(0);
    5937             : }
    5938             : 
    5939             : /*
    5940             :  * Parse a SQL datatype name and produce a PLpgSQL_type structure.

    5942             :  * The heavy lifting is done elsewhere.  Here we are only concerned
    5943             :  * with setting up an errcontext link that will let us give an error
    5944             :  * cursor pointing into the plpgsql function source, if necessary.
    5945             :  * This is handled the same as in check_sql_expr(), and we likewise
    5946             :  * expect that the given string is a copy from the source text.
    5947             :  */

    5956             :

    5962             :     error_context_stack = &syntax_errcontext;
    5963             : 
    5964             :     /* Let the main parser try to parse it under standard SQL rules */

    5966             :     typenameTypeIdAndMod(NULL, typeName, &type_id, &typmod);

    5984             :     {

    6001             : /*
    6002             :  * Read the arguments (if any) for a cursor, followed by the until token
    6003             :  *
    6004             :  * If cursor has no args, just swallow the until token and return NULL.
